## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: classical mechanics (nonlinear oscillations / dynamical systems)
**Analysis**: The target dv_dt is acceleration expressed as a function of position x, velocity v, and possibly explicit time t, which is the standard second-order ODE form for (nonlinear) oscillators. Common models include restoring forces from a potential U(x), damping forces depending on v, and external/parametric forcing terms depending on t.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Simple harmonic oscillator (undamped): dv_dt = -c0 * x (linear restoring force)
- Linear damped oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v (viscous damping)
- Driven damped oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v + c2 * cos(c3 * t) (external periodic forcing)
- Duffing oscillator (cubic stiffness): dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**3 - c2 * v (hardening/softening spring nonlinearity)
- Driven Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**3 - c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (nonlinear resonance/chaos)
- Pendulum equation (small-to-large angle): dv_dt = -c0 * sin(c1 * x) - c2 * v (nonlinear restoring from gravity)
- Parametrically excited oscillator: dv_dt = -(c0 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) * x - c3 * v (time-varying stiffness, Mathieu-type)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * (1 - c1 * x**2) * v - c2 * x (self-excited oscillations / limit cycle)
- Rayleigh oscillator (nonlinear damping in v): dv_dt = -c0 * x + (c1 - c2 * v**2) * v (amplitude-dependent dissipation/injection)
- Quadratic (aerodynamic) damping: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v - c2 * Abs(v) * v (drag-like dissipation)
- Nonlinear stiffness with quintic term: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**3 - c2 * x**5 - c3 * v (higher-order potential approximation)
- Mixed nonlinear coupling: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v - c2 * x**2 * v (state-dependent damping due to geometry/material effects)
- Asymmetric restoring force (broken symmetry): dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**2 - c2 * x**3 - c3 * v (offset/preload or asymmetric potential)
- State-dependent frequency (effective stiffness): dv_dt = -(c0 + c1 * x**2) * x - c2 * v (amplitude-dependent natural frequency)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Conservative oscillator structure: if damping/forcing are absent, dv_dt typically depends only on x as dv_dt = -dU/dx; polynomial U(x) leads to odd-power restoring terms (x, x**3, x**5).
- Symmetric potentials imply odd restoring force: dv_dt(x) changes sign with x (dominant terms x, x**3, ...); even powers (x**2) suggest asymmetry/bias.
- Viscous damping signature: a term proportional to -v indicates linear energy loss per cycle; additional -Abs(v)*v or -v**3 indicates amplitude-dependent dissipation.
- Self-excitation/limit-cycle indicator: damping that changes sign with amplitude (e.g., (1 - c*x**2)*v or (c1 - c2*v**2)*v) produces small-amplitude growth and large-amplitude decay.
- External periodic forcing: additive sin/cos terms in t inject energy at specific frequencies, enabling resonance peaks and phase-locked responses.
- Parametric resonance indicator: time-periodic modulation multiplying x (e.g., -(c0 + c1*cos(c2*t))*x) can destabilize the trivial solution near frequency ratios (Mathieu-like).
- Hardening vs softening stiffness: positive cubic stiffness in the restoring force (e.g., -x - x**3) generally shifts frequency upward with amplitude; negative cubic shifts it downward.
- Nonlinear coupling terms (x*v, x**2*v): imply state-dependent damping or geometry/material nonlinearities and often produce waveform distortion beyond simple sinusoidal motion.
- Pendulum-like nonlinearity: sin(c*x) restoring leads to near-linear behavior for small x but saturates for large x, producing amplitude-dependent period without polynomial divergence.

\[
-0.11806401595\,v(1-x^2)\;-\;1.00534224148\,v\;-\;0.502671120738\log(|v|+1)\;+\;0.342318903764\sin(t)\;-\;0.502671120738\sin(v)
\]
Key structural requirements that must be matched **exactly** (for all real \(x,v,t\)):

1) A mixed term \(v(1-x^2)=v - v x^2\), i.e. it contains a **\(v x^2\)** coupling.  
2) A \(\log(|v|+1)\) term: **log with Abs(v)** inside.  
3) A \(\sin(v)\) term.  
4) A \(\sin(t)\) term (cos allowed only if phase-shifted to sin).  
5) No other dependence (no exp, no log of \(t\) or \(x\), etc.).

### Summary of why none can match
Every candidate fails at least one **non-negotiable** GT feature:
- None contains the required **coupling term** \(-(\text{const})\,v x^2\) (they have at most linear \(x\) or \(x^{p}\) alone, never multiplied by \(v\)).
- None contains \(\sin(v)\).
- Candidates with logs use \(\log(c v+1)\) **without Abs**, which cannot equal \(\log(|v|+1)\) on a sign-changing \(v\) domain.

Therefore no parameter choices can make any candidate identical to the GT for all real \(x,v,t\).

GT: F0*sin(t) - beta*log(Abs(v) + c0) - beta*sin(v) - c1*beta*v - mu*(c2 - x**c3)*v

I need to compare each candidate against the Ground Truth (GT):

**GT:** `-0.118064*v*(1 - x²) - 1.00534*v - 0.502671*log(|v| + 1) + 0.342319*sin(t) - 0.502671*sin(v)`

Expanding: `0.118064*v*x² - 0.118064*v - 1.00534*v - 0.502671*log(|v| + 1) + 0.342319*sin(t) - 0.502671*sin(v)`

Simplifying: `0.118064*v*x² - 1.12340*v - 0.502671*log(|v| + 1) + 0.342319*sin(t) - 0.502671*sin(v)`

The GT contains these basis functions:
1. `v*x²` — a product of v and x²
2. `v` — linear in v
3. `log(|v| + 1)` — logarithm with absolute value
4. `sin(t)` — sine of t
5. `sin(v)` — sine of v

Key observations:
- The GT has `sin(v)` as a basis function
- The GT has `log(|v| + 1)` with absolute value
- The GT has `v*x²` (interaction term)
- No `cos(t)` term (though `sin(t)` can be written as `cos(t - π/2)`)
- `sin(t)` can be represented by `a*sin(t+b) + c*cos(t)` with appropriate constants

Let me check: `sin(t) = sin(1*t + 0)` can be matched by `c1*sin(c2*t + c3) + c9*cos(t)` by setting c2=1, c3=0, c9=0.

Now, the critical missing pieces in most candidates:
- **`sin(v)`**: This is essential and cannot be replicated by `v^c`, `exp(v)`, `log(v+1)`, or `v²`. Most candidates lack `sin(v)`.
- **`v*x²`**: This interaction term requires a product of v and a power of x. Most candidates have `x` linearly or not at all.
- **`log(|v|+1)`**: Needs absolute value; `log(c*v+1)` only works for v > -1/c.

Let me scan all candidates for `sin(v)`: None of the candidates contain `sin(v)` as a term.

Since `sin(v)` is a transcendental function of `v` that is linearly independent from all polynomial, exponential, and logarithmic functions of `v`, no combination of `v^c`, `exp(v)`, `log(v+1)`, `v²`, etc. can exactly reproduce `sin(v)` for all values of `v`.

Similarly, the `v*x²` interaction term requires a product structure that most candidates lack.

Since **none** of the candidates contain `sin(v)` and this term has a non-zero coefficient (-0.502671), and `sin(v)` cannot be expressed as any combination of the basis functions present in the candidates (polynomials in v, exponentials in v, logarithms in v, powers of x, etc.), **no candidate can match the GT**.

Let me verify this conclusion by checking each candidate:

Candidates 1-50: None contain `sin(v)`. The `-0.502671*sin(v)` term in the GT is linearly independent from all basis functions available in every candidate. Therefore, no candidate can match.
